## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics (rate laws / ODE modeling)
**Analysis**: The target dA_dt is the time-derivative of a species concentration A, which is the canonical setup for kinetic rate-law ODEs. With only (t, A) available, plausible models are single-species decay/production, approach-to-equilibrium, or time-varying effective rate constants driven by external conditions.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Zero-order kinetics: dA_dt = -c0 (rate independent of A; e.g., surface-limited or constant-flux removal)
- Constant source/sink: dA_dt = c0 - c1 (net constant production minus constant loss over the observed window)
- First-order kinetics: dA_dt = -c0 * A (unimolecular decay, radioactive/thermal decomposition in well-mixed limit)
- Second-order kinetics: dA_dt = -c0 * A**2 (bimolecular self-reaction or pseudo-second-order behavior)
- Nth-order (power-law) kinetics: dA_dt = -c0 * A**c1 (empirical order; chain reactions or complex mechanisms reduced to power law)
- Linear relaxation to equilibrium: dA_dt = -c0 * (A - c1) (approach to steady state A = c1; effective first-order in deviation)
- Autocatalytic / logistic-type kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (self-accelerating at low A with saturation/limitation at high A)
- Autocatalysis with background decay: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) - c2 * A (growth-like term opposed by first-order loss)
- Generalized inhibition/limited-rate form: dA_dt = -c0 * A / (1 + c1 * A**c2) (rate per concentration decreases at high A due to inhibition/crowding/transport limits)
- Time-varying rate coefficient (linear drift): dA_dt = -(c0 + c1 * t) * A (effective k(t) changes slowly over time due to temperature/catalyst drift)
- Time-varying rate coefficient (exponential drift): dA_dt = -c0 * exp(c1 * t) * A (accelerating or decelerating kinetics under systematic external change)
- Decaying activity (aging catalyst/quencher buildup): dA_dt = -c0 * exp(-c1 * t) * A (rate constant effectively decreases with time)
- Periodic forcing of kinetics: dA_dt = -c0 * (1 + c1 * sin(c2 * t)) * A (e.g., periodically modulated light/temperature affecting an effective first-order loss)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- If dA_dt is proportional to A (straight line when plotting dA_dt vs A through origin), a first-order law dA_dt ≈ -c0*A is likely.
- If dA_dt scales like a power of A (linear when plotting log(-dA_dt) vs log(A)), an nth-order form -c0*A**c1 is suggested.
- A nonzero dA_dt at A ≈ 0 indicates a constant source/sink term (additive c0) rather than pure decay proportional to A.
- A stable nonzero concentration where dA_dt crosses zero implies an equilibrium/steady state; structures like -c0*(A-c1) encode that directly.
- Sigmoidal time evolution of A (slow-fast-slow) is often produced by autocatalytic terms like c0*A*(c1-A), not by simple first-order decay.
- Strong curvature where increases in A do not proportionally increase -dA_dt suggests inhibition/limited-rate rational forms such as -c0*A/(1+c1*A**c2).
- Systematic trend of apparent rate over time at fixed A indicates k depends on t; try k(t) as (c0+c1*t), exp(c1*t), or exp(-c1*t).
- Oscillations in dA_dt at similar A values across different times indicate periodic forcing in time (sin/cos modulation of an effective rate).

GT Equivalence Verification (CRK10)
============================================================
GT: -c0*A**c1 + c2*_t*sin(log(A + c3))
Candidate formulas: 78

GT is the fixed function (independent of \(t\)):
\[
f(A)= -0.17495597007573369\,A^2 \;+\; 0.59132419335575606\,\sin(\log(A+1)).
\]
So any matching candidate must be reducible (by choosing its free constants, and possibly restricting domain) to “quadratic in \(A\) + sine of \(\log(A+1)\)” with **no remaining \(t\)-dependence**, and with **no extra terms** (no linear \(A\), no rational-in-\(A\) leftovers, no extra logs, etc.). Also note \(\log(A+1)\) requires domain \(A>-1\). If a candidate uses \(\log(c\cdot|A|+1)\), we can match \(\log(A+1)\) under the plausible condition \(A\ge 0\) by setting \(c=1\).

Below, for each candidate, I check whether it can be tuned to exactly the GT form (possibly under a domain condition like \(A\ge 0\)).

---

### 1.
Only rational terms in \(A\) of form \(A\cdot(\text{const}) + A/(\text{poly}+1)\). No sine term at all. Cannot match GT. **No**.

### 2.
\[
A c_0 + c_1\log(c_2|A|+1)+ c_3\sin(c_4\log(c_5|A|+1)+c_6)
\]
Has a sine-of-log part (good), but **no \(A^2\) term**; also has unavoidable extra \(A\) and/or \(\log\) unless set to 0. If set \(c_0=0,c_1=0\), we get only sine-of-log, still missing \(-0.1749A^2\). **No**.

### 3.
All terms divided by \(A+c_1\). GT has no such denominator. Only way is to make numerator proportional to \(A+c_1\) exactly, but numerator contains \(A^2\) and \(A\log(\cdot)\) etc; cannot become \((A+c_1)\big(-kA^2 + s\sin(\log(A+1))\big)\) because there is no sine, only logs. **No**.

### 4.
Polynomial + terms like \(\log(\cdot)/A\) and \(1/A\). No sine. Also singular at 0 unlike GT. **No**.

### 5.
Rational with common denominator \(A^{c_0}c_2+1\) and only logs, no sine. **No**.

### 6.
Rational with denominator \(A^2c_1+1\) and logs, no sine. **No**.

### 7.
Rational over \(A+c_1\) with logs, no sine. **No**.

### 8.
Has \(A c_0\), a rational term \(A^{c_1}c_2/(A^{c_1}+c_3)\), and a log term. No sine. **No**.

### 9.
Linear + rational + log. No sine, no \(A^2\). **No**.

### 10.
Linear + rational + log. No sine, no \(A^2\). **No**.

### 11.
Quadratic + linear + logs (including \(\log(c_5 e^{Ac_6}+1)\)). No sine. **No**.

### 12.
Quadratic + rational terms + \(c_6 e^{c_7|A|}\cos(c_8 t)\). GT has sine(log(A+1)) and no \(t\). You could kill the cosine term by \(c_6=0\), but then there is still no sine(log). **No**.

### 13.
Everything over \(A+c_1\) and has sine(log) pieces in numerator. But GT has **no denominator**. To remove denominator you’d need the whole expression to equal GT for all \(A\) in a domain, which would force \((A+c_1)\cdot GT\) to be representable by the available numerator structure. Numerator here is at most \(A^2\) plus \(A\sin(\log(\cdot))\) plus \(\sin(\log(\cdot))\), i.e. it cannot produce \((A+c_1)(-kA^2 + s\sin(\log(A+1))) = -kA^3 -kc_1A^2 + sA\sin(\cdot)+ sc_1\sin(\cdot)\) because there is **no \(A^3\) term available** in the numerator. So cannot cancel denominator to match a quadratic+ sine. **No**.

### 14.
Purely rational in \(|A|\) with denominator \(c_1|A|+|A|^2\), no sine. **No**.

### 15.
Quadratic + linear + rational power term \(A^{c_4}c_5/(A^{c_4}+c_6)\). No sine(log). **No**.

### 16.
Quadratic + linear + rational terms. No sine(log). **No**.

### 17.
Quadratic + linear + rational + power \(A^{c_6}c_7\). No sine(log). **No**.

### 18.
All over \(A+c_1\) with logs, no sine. Also would have \(A^3\) structure. **No**.

### 19.
Quadratic + linear + constant/power/rational, no sine(log). **No**.

### 20.
Quadratic + linear + rational terms, no sine(log). **No**.

### 21.
All over \(A+c_1\) with logs, no sine. **No**.

### 22.
All over \(A+c_1\) with logs, no sine. **No**.

### 23.
Quadratic + linear + constant + rational terms, no sine(log). **No**.

### 24.
Quadratic + linear + rational terms, no sine(log). **No**.

### 25.
Quadratic + linear + terms like \(A c_2/(1+c_3/A)\) (which is rational) etc. No sine(log). **No**.

### 26.
Linear + rational + \(A^{c_4}c_5\log(\cdot)\). No sine. **No**.

### 27.
Quadratic + linear + rational + \(A^{c_6}c_7\log(Ac_8+1)\). No sine. **No**.

### 28.
Quadratic + quadratic + linear + rational terms, no sine(log). **No**.

### 29.
Quadratic + linear + log + \(|A|\log\). No sine. **No**.

### 30.

### 31.
\[
A^2c_0 + Ac_1 + A\frac{c_2}{A+c_3} + c_4\sin(c_5\log(c_6|A|+1)+c_7)
\]
This has the needed **quadratic** and **sine-of-log** (good). But it also has extra terms \(Ac_1\) and \(A c_2/(A+c_3)\). We can set \(c_1=0\) and \(c_2=0\) to remove them. Then we get:
\[
A^2c_0 + c_4\sin(c_5\log(c_6|A|+1)+c_7).
\]
Now match exactly under domain \(A\ge 0\):
- Set \(c_0=-0.17495597007573369\).
- Want \(\sin(\log(A+1))\): choose \(c_6=1\) so \(\log(c_6|A|+1)=\log(A+1)\) for \(A\ge 0\).
- Set \(c_5=1\), \(c_7=0\) so argument is \(\log(A+1)\).
- Set \(c_4=0.59132419335575606\).

This yields exactly GT on the plausible continuous domain \(A\ge 0\) (and also respects \(A>-1\)). **Yes, candidate 31 matches (conditional on \(A\ge 0\)).**
